Refuting the Objection: Effecterness is Not the Effect Itself
Razi refutes the objection and argues effecterness is positive.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the refutation of the counter-objection that equates effecterness with the effect's existence, and why effecterness must be a positive attribute.

Core Idea
Effecterness cannot be the effect itself; it is a positive attribute distinct from essence.

After presenting the four proofs, the author anticipates a potential objection: perhaps 'being an effecter' is simply the occurrence of the effect. This lesson explores the refutation of that objection and the subsequent argument that the attribute of effecterness is a positive (thubuti) attribute, not a negative one.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and refutation
Read the Arabic passage from 'لا يقال' to 'زائدا على الذات'. Understand the objection and the refutation.
2
Understand the refutation
The refutation shows that equating effecterness with the effect leads to circular causality: the effect would be the cause of itself.
3
Learn the positive attribute argument
The text then argues that effecterness is positive because its negation is pure negation, so the positive must be additional.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Commentary
This passage presents the second philosophical objection against the Ash'ari doctrine of the world's creation. Imam Razi begins by stating the philosophers' claim: the concept of the Necessary Being being an 'effecter' (mu'aththir) in the world is something additional (mugheyir) both to the essence of the Necessary Existent and to the essence of the world. He then lists four proofs (wujuh) they offer. First proof: we can conceive the two essences while doubting the effecterness, showing it is additional. Second proof: effecterness is a relation between two things, and a relation is dependent on its relata, so it is additional. Third proof: we predicate effecterness of the essence, and what is predicated is other than the subject. Fourth proof: effecterness can be renewed (tajaddud) while the essence persists, showing it is additional. Then Razi presents a potential objection (la yuqalu): perhaps 'being an effecter' is nothing but the very occurrence of the effect. He refutes this: if that were so, then explaining the effect's existence by the effecter's effecterness would be explaining a thing by itself, which is impossible. He then argues that this attribute must be positive (thubuti), not negative, because its negation is pure negation. Finally, he draws the theological consequence: God's effecterness is either originated or eternal. If originated, an infinite regress follows. So it must be eternal. But effecterness is a relational attribute (sifa idafiyya) requiring the existence of both relata; if it is eternal, the effect must also be eternal. Thus the philosophers conclude that the world is pre-eternal (qadim). Razi presents this as an objection to be refuted later.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that the attribute of effecterness is negative or merely a relation without extra reality.
Correction: The text shows that effecterness is a positive extra attribute because its negation is pure negation, and it cannot be reduced to the effect itself.

Checkpoint
What is the flaw in equating effecterness with the existence of the effect?
A) It leads to infinite regress
B) It leads to circular causality
C) It denies the attribute
D) It contradicts the four proofs

Key Takeaway
Effecterness is a positive attribute additional to the essence, not reducible to the effect and not a mere negation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see an answer to a prayer in your life, do you ever reduce God's role to merely the outcome itself, forgetting the distinct act of His effecting? How does this argument call you to praise Him not just for what you receive, but for His real, ongoing causal involvement? What will you do today to acknowledge His effecterness as a separate, positive reality?
?
If God's effecterness were just the effect, then your gratitude would be for the thing, not for the Giver. Does your heart sometimes treat blessings as if they just happen, rather than being constantly effected by God? How can you train yourself to see every moment as a direct, fresh act of His causation?
?
This lesson insists that God's effect on the world is a real, additional attribute—not a mere absence of inability. Have you ever thought of God's power as just 'not being weak' rather than as a positive, dynamic force? What changes in your trust in Him when you realize His effecterness is not a negation but a vibrant, ever-present activity?

The Dilemma: Originated vs. Eternal Effecterness and the Pre-Eternity of the World
Razi presents the dilemma leading to the world's pre-eternity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the philosophers' argument that if effecterness is eternal, the world must also be eternal, implying pre-eternity.

Core Idea
An eternal effecterness requires an eternal effect, so the world is pre-eternal.

After establishing that effecterness is a positive additional attribute, the next step is to consider its temporal status. If it is originated, an infinite regress follows; if it is eternal, then as a relational attribute, it requires an eternal effect. This leads to the philosophical conclusion that the world is pre-eternal. This lesson examines that chain of reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the dilemma
Read the Arabic passage from 'ثم نقول' to the end. Pay attention to the two branches.
2
Explore the 'originated' branch
If effecterness is originated, it needs a cause, leading to an infinite regress (tasalsul) of causes.
Tasalsul is impossible per philosophers.
3
Explore the 'eternal' branch
If eternal, since effecterness is a relational attribute, the effect must coexist eternally.
4
Understand the conclusion
Thus the philosophers conclude that the world is pre-eternal (qadim).
This contradicts Islamic doctrine.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والشبهة الثانية لهم في هذه المسألة : قالوا : المفهوم من كون الواجب مؤثرًا في العالم أمر مغاير لذات واجب الوجود، ولذات العالم، ويدل عليه وجوه : أحدها: أنه يمكننا أن نعقل ذات واجب الوجود ونعقل ذات العالم مع الشك في أن واجب الوجود مؤثر في العالم، ومع الشك في أن ذات العالم أثر واجب الوجود، وإذا أمكن تعقل الذاتين حال كون المؤثرية مجهولة، علمنا أن كون الواجب مؤثرًا في وجود العالم وكون العالم أثرًا لواجب الوجود أمر مغاير للذاتين. وثانيها : إن كون أحد الذاتين مؤثرة في الأخرى نسبة بين الذاتين، والنسبة بين الشيئين متوقفة عليهما، والمتوقف على الشيء مغاير له، فهذه المؤثرية والأثرية وصفان مغايران للذاتين . وثالثها: أنا نقول هذه الذات مؤثرة في تلك فنحكم على تلك الذات بالمؤثرية، والمحكوم عليه مغاير للمحكوم به لا محالة. ورابعها : أنا نقول : هذه الذات صارت مؤثرة في الأثر الفلاني، بعد أن كانت غير مؤثرة فيه، فتجدد صفة المؤثرية مع كون الذات موجودة قبل يدل على أن صفة المؤثرية مغايرة لتلك الذات. لا يقال : لم لا يجوز أن يكون المراد من كونها مؤثرة في ذلك الأثر نفس حصول ذلك الأثر؟ لأنا نقول : هذا باطل، فإنا نقول : إنما وجد هذا الأثر لأجل أن هذا المؤثر أثر في وجوده فعللنا وجوده لمؤثرية المؤثر فيه، فلو كانت مؤثرية المؤثر عبارة عن وجود الأثر لكان ذلك تعليلا لوجود الأثر بنفسه، وإنه محال، وإذا ثبت أن كون واجب الوجود مؤثرًا في وجود العالم وصف زائد على الذات فنقول: هذا الوصف لا جائز أن يكون وصفًا سلبياً؛ لأن قولنا : الشيء الفلاني أثر في كذا، نقيض لقولنا : إنه ما أثر في كذا ولما كان قولنا : ما أثر في كذا سلبًا محضاً وجب أن يكون قولنا : إنه أثر في كذا وصفًا ثبوتيًا زائدا على الذات. ثم نقول : كون الله تعالى مؤثرًا في وجود العالم إما أن يكون حادثا أو قديماً، فإن كان حادثًا افتقر إلى محدث فكانت مؤثرية المؤثر في إحداث تلك المؤثرية زائدا عليه فيلزم التسلسل، فإذن مؤثرية الله تعالى في العالم صفة قديمة، ولكن كون الشيء مؤثرًا في غيره، صفة إضافية لا يعقل ثبوتها إلا مع ثبوت المضافين، فإذن كون الشيء موصوفًا بصفة المؤثرية من غير وجود الأثر محال عقلاً ، وإذا كانت صفة المؤثرية قديمة يلزم كون الأثر قديماً، وذلك يوجب القول بقدم الآثار.
And the second objection for them in this issue: They said: The concept of the Necessary Being being an effecter in the world is an matter additional to the essence of the Necessary Existent and to the essence of the world. And evidence for it is aspects: One of them: that we can conceive the essence of the Necessary Existent and conceive the essence of the world while being doubtful that the Necessary Existent is an effecter in the world, and while being doubtful that the essence of the world is an effect of the Necessary Existent. And when it is possible to conceive the two essences while the attribute of being an effecter is unknown, we know that the Necessary Being being an effecter in the existence of the world and the world being an effect of the Necessary Existent is an matter additional to the two essences. And the second of them: That one of the two essences being effecter in the other is a relation between the two essences, and the relation between two things is dependent upon them, and that which is dependent upon a thing is additional to it, so this effecterness and effectness are two attributes additional to the two essences. And the third of them: We say: This essence is effecter in that, so we judge upon that essence with effecterness, and the thing judged upon is additional to the thing judged with necessarily. And the fourth of them: We say: This essence became effecter in such an effect after it was not effecter in it, so the attribute of effecterness is renewed while the essence exists before, indicating that the attribute of effecterness is additional to that essence. It should not be said: Why is it not permissible that what is meant by it being effecter in that effect is the very occurrence of that effect? Because we say: This is false, for we say: This effect only came to be because this effecter effected in its existence, so we caused its existence to be for the effecterness of the effecter in it. So if the effecterness of the effecter were an expression for the existence of the effect, that would be a causation of the existence of the effect by itself, and that is impossible. And when it is established that the Necessary Existent being an effecter in the existence of the world is an attribute additional to the essence, we say: This attribute may not be a negative attribute; because our saying: 'This thing is an effect in such-and-such' is the contradictory of our saying: 'It is not an effect in such-and-such'. And since our saying: 'It is not an effect in such-and-such' is pure negation, it is necessary that our saying: 'It is an effect in such-and-such' is a positive attribute additional to the essence. Then we say: God Most High being an effecter in the existence of the world is either originated or eternal. If it is originated, it needs an originator, so the effecterness of the effecter in bringing about that effecterness would be additional to it, leading to infinite regress. Therefore, God's effecterness in the world is an eternal attribute. But a thing being an effecter in another is a relational attribute, whose existence is not conceivable except with the existence of the two relata. Therefore, a thing being described with the attribute of effecterness without the existence of the effect is rationally impossible. And if the attribute of effecterness is eternal, the effect must be eternal, and that necessitates the assertion of the pre-eternity of the effects.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage presents the second philosophical objection against the Ash'ari doctrine of the world's creation. Imam Razi begins by stating the philosophers' claim: the concept of the Necessary Being being an 'effecter' (mu'aththir) in the world is something additional (mugheyir) both to the essence of the Necessary Existent and to the essence of the world. He then lists four proofs (wujuh) they offer. First proof: we can conceive the two essences while doubting the effecterness, showing it is additional. Second proof: effecterness is a relation between two things, and a relation is dependent on its relata, so it is additional. Third proof: we predicate effecterness of the essence, and what is predicated is other than the subject. Fourth proof: effecterness can be renewed (tajaddud) while the essence persists, showing it is additional. Then Razi presents a potential objection (la yuqalu): perhaps 'being an effecter' is nothing but the very occurrence of the effect. He refutes this: if that were so, then explaining the effect's existence by the effecter's effecterness would be explaining a thing by itself, which is impossible. He then argues that this attribute must be positive (thubuti), not negative, because its negation is pure negation. Finally, he draws the theological consequence: God's effecterness is either originated or eternal. If originated, an infinite regress follows. So it must be eternal. But effecterness is a relational attribute (sifa idafiyya) requiring the existence of both relata; if it is eternal, the effect must also be eternal. Thus the philosophers conclude that the world is pre-eternal (qadim). Razi presents this as an objection to be refuted later.

Key Terms
حادث (hadith)
قديم (qadim)
التسلسل (tasalsul)
الصفة الإضافية (sifa idafiyya)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that an eternal attribute does not require an eternal effect because God could be eternally powerful without creating.
Correction: The argument specifically concerns the relational attribute of effecterness, which by definition requires an effect. An eternal power without an effect is not the same.

Checkpoint
What is the consequence if the attribute of effecterness is eternal?
A) It leads to infinite regress
B) The effect must also be eternal
C) The attribute becomes negative
D) The world is created

Key Takeaway
The philosophers argue that an eternal effecterness necessitates an eternal effect, implying the pre-eternity of the world.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the philosophers' argument seems logically airtight, yet you believe the world is created, what is the intellectual basis for your belief? Are you relying on revelation alone, or do you have a rational response? Search your heart: is your faith in creation based on certainty or comfort?
?
This argument depends on God's effecterness being an eternal attribute. Do you ever think of God as being compelled to act because of His attributes? How does the concept of God's free will (mashi'a) confront this philosophical necessity? Examine your own prayers and supplications: do you truly believe God could have chosen not to create?
?
The concept of a relational attribute is abstract, yet it shapes your entire worldview. In your daily life, do you treat your relationships (e.g., with family, colleagues) as merely accidental or as essential to who you are? What does this lesson teach you about dependency and existence?

The Philosophers' Proof from God's Eternal Effectiveness
Philosophers argue that God's eternal effectiveness necessitates an eternal world.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the philosophical argument that God's eternal attribute of effectiveness necessitates an eternal world, and the logical steps used to support it.

Core Idea
A relational attribute demands its relata; thus an eternal effect requires an eternal effect.

This passage presents a key argument used by philosophers to prove the eternity of the world. It examines the nature of God's attribute of being an 'effecter' (مؤثر) and argues that since this attribute is eternal and relational, the effect (the world) must also be eternal. Let's follow the logical steps carefully.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the argument's structure
The passage is a continuous chain of reasoning. First, it establishes that God's effectiveness is an attribute additional to His essence, not identical to the world's existence.
This avoids circularity.
2
Distinguish between attribute and effect
Notice the distinction: the effect's existence is explained by the effecter's effectiveness, but the effectiveness itself is not the same as the effect. This is crucial.
3
Analyze the regress argument
The attribute of effectiveness cannot be originated because that would lead to infinite regress. Therefore, it must be eternal.
Think about why an originated attribute would require another originator.
4
Understand the relational attribute reasoning
Effectiveness is a relational attribute that cannot exist without both the effecter and the effect. Since the attribute is eternal, the effect must be eternal as well.
This is the core of the argument for the world's eternity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقدمة الثالثة
هذا المؤثر أثر في وجوده فعللنا وجوده لمؤثرية المؤثر فيه، فلو كانت مؤثرية المؤثر عبارة عن وجود الأثر لكان ذلك تعليلا لوجود الأثر بنفسه، وإنه محال، وإذا ثبت أن كون واجب الوجود مؤثرًا في وجود العالم وصف زائد على الذات فنقول: هذا الوصف لا جائز أن يكون وصفًا سلبياً؛ لأن قولنا : الشيء الفلاني اثر في كذا، نقيض لقولنا : إنه ما أثر في كذا ولما كان قولنا : ما أثر في كذا سلبًا محضاً وجب أن يكون قولنا : إنه أثر في كذا وصفًا ثبوتيًا زائدا على الذات.
ثم نقول : كون الله تعالى مؤثرًا في وجود العالم إما أن يكون حادثا أو قديماً، فإن كان حادثًا افتقر إلى محدث فكانت مؤثرية المؤثر في إحداث تلك المؤثرية زائدا عليه فيلزم التسلسل، فإذن مؤثرية الله تعالى في العالم صفة قديمة، ولكن كون الشيء مؤثرًا في غيره، صفة إضافية لا يعقل ثبوتها إلا مع ثبوت المضافين، فإذن كون الشيء موصوفًا بصفة المؤثرية من غير وجود الأثر محال عقلاً ، وإذا كانت صفة المؤثرية قديمة يلزم كون الأثر قديماً، وذلك يوجب القول بقدم الآثار.
The third introduction: This effecter had an effect in its existence, so we explained its existence by the effecter's effectiveness in it. If the effecter's effectiveness were identical to the existence of the effect, that would be explaining the existence of the effect by itself, which is impossible. And when it is established that the Necessary Existent's being an effecter in the existence of the world is an attribute additional to the essence, we say: This attribute cannot be a negative attribute; because our statement 'that thing had an effect in such-and-such' is the contradictory of our statement 'it did not have an effect in such-and-such'. And since our statement 'it did not have an effect in such-and-such' is pure negation, it is necessary that our statement 'it had an effect in such-and-such' be a positive attribute additional to the essence. Then we say: God's being an effecter in the existence of the world is either originated or eternal. If it is originated, it needs an originator, so the effecter's effectiveness in causing that effectiveness would be additional to it, leading to infinite regress. Therefore, God's effectiveness in the world is an eternal attribute. But a thing's being an effecter in something else is a relational attribute; its subsistence is inconceivable except with the subsistence of the two relata. Therefore, a thing being described with the attribute of effectiveness without the existence of the effect is rationally impossible. And if the attribute of effectiveness is eternal, the effect must be eternal, and that necessitates the statement that the effects are eternal.
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage is an argument (presented as a third introduction) for the eternity of the world from the nature of God's attribute of being an effecter (مؤثرية). First, it establishes that the effecter's effectiveness is not identical to the effect's existence, because that would be circular. Instead, it is a positive attribute additional to the divine essence. It then examines whether this attribute is originated or eternal. If originated, it would require another originator, leading to an infinite regress. So it must be eternal. But effectiveness is a relational attribute (صفة إضافية) that cannot exist without both relata (the effecter and the effect). Therefore, if the attribute is eternal, the effect must also be eternal. Consequently, the world (the effect) is eternal. The argument proceeds step by step, using logical distinctions between positive and negative attributes, and between essential and relational attributes.

Key Terms
مؤثر
مؤثرية
واجب الوجود
وصف ثبوتي
صفة إضافية
قدم
أثر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that God's attribute of being a creator is identical to His essence (as Ash'aris hold), but this argument assumes it is additional. Also, one might think that a relational attribute can exist without the effect, but the argument says it cannot.
Correction: The argument explicitly states that effectiveness is a positive attribute additional to the essence and that it is relational, requiring the existence of the effect.

Checkpoint
According to this argument, why must the effect (the world) be eternal?
A) Because God's attribute of effectiveness is positive.
B) Because effectiveness is a relational attribute that requires the coexistence of the effect, and the attribute is eternal.
C) Because the world cannot be originated.
D) Because God's essence necessitates the world's existence.

Key Takeaway
The philosophers argue that God's eternal effectiveness as a relational attribute forces the world to be eternal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's attribute of being an effecter necessarily requires an eternal effect, then the world has always existed. Does your heart accept that the universe is co-eternal with God? Or does something in your iman resist that? What is that resistance, and how does this passage challenge it?
?
The philosophers argue that if God's effectiveness were originated, it would need another cause, leading to infinite regress. But do you live as though God's attributes are created or uncreated? When you think of God's power, do you treat it as something that started at some point, or as eternal without beginning? How does your daily worship reflect that belief?
?
This passage forces a radical conclusion: the effect (the world) must exist as long as the attribute exists. If you truly believed the world is necessary and eternal (like the philosophers), how would that change your sense of urgency in seeking God? Would you feel less dependent on Him? Or would it deepen your awareness of His constant, necessary action?

The Fifth Doubt: Beneficence and Eternal Causality
Two formulations of the fifth doubt: moral and causal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two philosophical arguments that attempt to prove the eternity of the world from God's beneficence and His necessary causality.

Core Idea
If God is eternally generous and the cause of the world, the world must also be eternal.

In this passage, Imam al-Razi presents the fifth doubt of the philosophers against the Islamic doctrine of temporal creation. The doubt comes in two forms: one based on God's attribute of beneficence, and the other on the principle of causality. The philosophers aim to show that God's eternal nature necessitates an eternal world. Understanding these arguments is crucial for grasping the Islamic response.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Notice the two formulations: one moral (beneficence), one causal.
The passage uses very precise causal language.
2
Identify the two arguments
The first says creation is beneficence; if God delayed it, He would be ungenerous for eternity. The second says the cause (God's existence) is eternal, so the effect (world) must also be eternal.
3
Reflect on the assumptions
The arguments assume that creation is necessarily an act of beneficence and that an eternal cause must have an eternal effect. Consider whether these assumptions are valid.
These are key points for later rebuttal.
4
Compare the formulations
How are the two arguments similar? How do they differ in their premises?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشبهة الخامسة لهم : قالوا : الإيجاد إحسان، فلو لم يكن الله تعالى موجدا في الأزل لكان تاركًا للجود والإحسان، مدة غير متناهية، وذلك غير جائز، وربما عبروا بعبارة أخرى فقالوا : علة وجود العالم وجود الباري تعالى ووجود الباري تعالى أزلي، فيلزم أن يكون وجود العالم أزليا.
The fifth doubt of them: They said: Bringing into existence is beneficence. If God were not bringing into existence in eternity, He would be abandoning generosity and beneficence for an infinite duration, and that is not permissible. And perhaps they express it with another expression: They say: The cause of the existence of the world is the existence of God Most High, and the existence of God Most High is eternal. Therefore, it follows that the existence of the world is eternal.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage presents the fifth doubt in two formulations. The first is moral: creation (إيجاد) is an act of beneficence (إحسان). If God were not creating from eternity (في الأزل), He would be failing to be generous for an infinite period, which is incompatible with His perfection. The second is causal: The cause (علة) of the world's existence is God's existence, and God's existence is eternal (أزلي). An eternal cause must have an eternal effect, so the world must be eternal. Both formulations aim to show that God's eternal nature necessitates an eternal world.

Key Terms
إيجاد
إحسان
جود
علة
أزلي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that the argument is about God's power to create at any time, but it actually assumes that creation is a necessary act of beneficence, not a free choice.
Correction: The argument treats creation as a necessary expression of generosity, not a voluntary act that could be delayed.

Checkpoint
In the second formulation of this doubt, why must the world be eternal?
A) Because God is generous.
B) Because the cause of the world is God's existence, which is eternal.
C) Because God cannot change.
D) Because the world is perfect.

Key Takeaway
The philosophers argue that God's eternal beneficence and causality necessitate an eternal world.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that God's beneficence is voluntary and unconstrained, or do you sometimes feel that God 'must' give you something because He is good? How does this passage challenge your assumption?
?
Consider the causal chain: if God is the cause of everything, and He is eternal, where does that leave your own free will? Are you merely an effect of an eternal cause, or is there a different relationship?
?
When you think about your own acts of generosity, do you give freely or because you feel compelled? What does this passage's argument about God's 'necessary' beneficence reveal about your own heart?

The Sixth Doubt: Philosophers' Argument Against Divine Choice
Al-Razi presents and rebuts the sixth doubt of the philosophers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the philosophical argument that God cannot act by choice and why theologians refute it by showing the dilemma of preference or equality.

Core Idea
If God's act is preferable, He changes; if equal, no reason to choose.

The philosophers raise a powerful doubt: if God creates the world in time, He must act by choice. But acting by choice seems to require a reason that either makes the act preferable or leaves it equal. Both options lead to absurdities. In this passage, Imam al-Razi presents their argument and the theological response, showing why the dilemma fails.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the literal translation to grasp the argument's flow.
Notice the logical structure: entailment, then proof of impossibility, then objection and reply.
2
Identify the two horns of the dilemma
The argument presents two possibilities: either the act is preferable for God, or the alternatives are equal. Understand each horn and why it is claimed to be impossible.
The first horn implies change and imperfection; the second makes choice impossible.
3
Analyze the objection and its refutation
The objection suggests that beneficence to others makes the act preferable without change. See how al-Razi responds by showing the same problem recurs.
The response applies the same dilemma to beneficence itself.
4
Connect to the larger debate
Reflect on how this argument is used to support the eternity of the world. The theologians reject it by affirming that God's will is eternal and His choice does not imply change.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الشبهة السادسة لهم قالوا : لو كان الباري تعالى موجدًا للعالم بعد أن لم يكن موجدًا له لكان فاعلا بالاختيار وهذا محال فذاك محال، أما الملازمة فبينة بذاتها، ومتفق عليها، وأما أن التالي محال فلآن من قصد إلى إيجاد شيء فإما أن يكون ذلك الإيجاد أولى بالنسبة إليه من ترك الإيجاد وإما أن يكون طرفاه متساويين، والأول محال ؛ لأن قبل ذلك الإيجاد ما كانت تلك الأولوية حاصلة، وعند الإيجاد حصلت تلك الأولوية، فيلزم منه أن يكون ناقصا لذاته، مستكملا بغيره، وهذا محال، وأما إن لم يكن الفعل أولى بالنسبة إليه من الترك امتنع أن يرجح الفعل على الترك؛ لأن الترجيح والاستواء ضدان والجمع بينهما محال.
لا يقال : الفعل وإن لم يكن أولى من الترك بالنسبة إلى ذلك الفعل إلا أنه أولى بالنسبة إلى غيره ؛ لأن الإيجاد إحسان إلى الغير، وهذا القدر من الرجحان كافٍ في ترجيح الفعل على الترك ؛ لأنا نقول : إيصال الإحسان إلى الغير إن كان أولى بالنسبة إليه من عدمه عاد حديث النقص الذاتي، وإن لم يكن أولى عاد حديث الاستواء، والله الهادي.
The sixth doubt of them: They said: If God were to bring the world into existence after having not brought it into existence, then He would be an agent by choice, and that is impossible, so the former is impossible. As for the entailment, it is evident in itself and agreed upon. As for the impossible nature of the consequent, it is because one who intends to bring something into existence, either that bringing into existence is preferable for him to refraining from bringing into existence, or the two alternatives are equal. The first is impossible because before that bringing into existence, that preference was not present, and at the time of bringing into existence, that preference arose. This would imply that He was imperfect in Himself, becoming complete through another, which is impossible. As for if the act is not preferable to refraining, it is impossible for Him to give preponderance to the act over refraining, because preponderance and equality are opposites and combining them is impossible. It cannot be said: Even if the act is not preferable to refraining with respect to that act, it is preferable with respect to something else, because bringing into existence is beneficence to another, and this degree of preponderance is sufficient for giving preponderance to the act over refraining. For we say: If conveying beneficence to another is preferable for Him to not doing so, then the issue of essential imperfection returns. If it is not preferable, then the issue of equality returns. And God is the Guide.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage presents the sixth doubt, which argues that God cannot be an agent by choice (فاعل بالاختيار), because acting by choice would require either a reason for preference or equality. If the act is preferable, then that preference must arise at the moment of action, implying change in God from not having preference to having it, which would mean He was imperfect and became perfect through another—impossible for God. If the alternatives are equal, then there is no basis for preferring one over the other, making choice impossible. The argument then addresses a potential objection: perhaps the act is preferable because it benefits others. The response is that if beneficence is preferable for God, the same problem of acquired perfection arises; if not, equality remains. Thus, God cannot act by choice, so if the world were created in time, God would have to choose, which is impossible; therefore the world must be eternal.

Key Terms
اختيار
فاعل بالاختيار
أولوية
ترجيح
استواء
إحسان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that God's choice is based on wisdom without change, but the argument assumes any new preference implies change.
Correction: The theologians affirm that God's will is eternal and His choice does not require a new attribute; the philosophers' assumption of change is false.

Checkpoint
According to this argument, what would it imply if the act of creation were preferable for God?
A) That God is generous.
B) That God would be imperfect in Himself and completed by another.
C) That God's will is eternal.
D) That the world must be eternal.

Key Takeaway
The philosophers' argument that God cannot act by choice fails because it wrongly assumes that any new preference implies change in God's essence, while theologians affirm God's eternal will and choice without change.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's act of creation does not depend on any external benefit or preference, how does that challenge your tendency to think that God must always act for a reason you can understand? When you face a trial, do you secretly doubt God's goodness because you cannot see the benefit?
?
The philosophers argued that a new decision in God implies imperfection. Have you ever felt that God's commands are arbitrary or that He changes His mind? How can this lesson root out that subtle disrespect from your heart?
?
You know that God is completely self-sufficient, yet you often act as if your obedience adds something to Him. Reflect: Do you ever serve God expecting something in return, as if He needs your worship? How can you today purify your intention to worship Him for His sake alone, not for any personal gain?

Why Efficacy Is Not an Added Attribute
Razi refutes that the agent's efficacy is an added attribute via reductio.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's proof that an agent's efficacy cannot be a separate attribute, and how this avoids infinite regress.

Core Idea
If efficacy were an added attribute, it would need its own agent—leading to an endless chain.

Imam Razi addresses a common doubt: is the power to cause effects a distinct attribute added to the agent's essence? If it were, that attribute itself would be contingent and require another agent, leading to infinite regress. In this passage, Razi shows why the efficacy must be identical with the essence or a necessary concomitant.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then its literal translation. Let Razi's own words establish the argument.
Notice the conditional structure: 'if it were so... then...'
2
Understand key terms
Make sure you understand 'مؤثر' (agent), 'أثر' (effect), 'صفة زائدة' (added attribute), and 'التسلسل' (infinite regress).
These terms are central to the argument.
3
Follow the conditional logic
Razi argues: If efficacy is an added attribute, then it depends on the essence, so it is possible and needs an agent, which would require another efficacy, leading to infinite regress.
This is a reductio ad absurdum.
4
State the conclusion
The only way to avoid regress is that efficacy is not an added attribute but is identical with the essence or a necessary concomitant.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والجواب عن الشبهة الثانية: أنا نقول : مؤثرية المؤثر في الأثر لا يجوز أن تكون وصفا زائدا على ذات المؤثر؛ لأنه لو كان كذلك لكانت تلك الصفة مفتقرة في تحققها إلى ذات الموصوف فتكون ممكنة في ذاتها مفتقرة إلى المؤثر، فتكون مؤثرية المؤثر في ذات المؤثر زائدة عليها ويلزم التسلسل.
And the answer to the second doubt: We say: The agency of the agent in the effect (mu'aththariyyah al-mu'aththir fi al-athar) cannot be an attribute superadded to the essence of the agent; because if it were so, then that attribute would depend for its realization on the essence of the described, so it would be possible in itself, dependent on the agent, so the agency of the agent in the essence of the agent would be superadded upon it, and an infinite regress would follow.
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of a doubt that claims the agent's power or efficacy is an attribute added to its essence. Razi argues that if it were an added attribute, that attribute itself would be a possible thing needing an agent (since it depends on the essence it qualifies). This would require another agent for that attribute, and so on, leading to an infinite regress. Therefore, the efficacy must be identical with the essence or a necessary concomitant, not a separate attribute.

Key Terms
مؤثر
أثر
صفة زائدة
ذات
التسلسل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The agent's power to cause effects is a distinct attribute added to its essence.
Correction: If it were added, it would be contingent and require another agent, leading to infinite regress. Hence it is not added.

Checkpoint
According to Razi, why can't the agent's efficacy be an added attribute?
A) Because the attribute would be eternal
B) Because the attribute would be contingent and need another agent
C) Because the attribute would be self-sufficient
D) Because the attribute would negate free will

Key Takeaway
Razi's argument shows that to avoid infinite regress, an agent's efficacy must be identical with its essence or a necessary concomitant, not a separate attribute.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you believe your ability to pray, give charity, or do good deeds is your own separate power, how does Razi's argument expose that this belief leads to an infinite chain of causes? Are there areas where you attribute your spiritual successes to your own 'added' efficacy rather than to God? Write one concrete way you will remind yourself tomorrow that your power is not your possession but a direct gift from the One who is the source of all efficacy.
?
Razi shows that treating efficacy as a separate attribute leads to an endless regress of agents. In your life, do you seek multiple intermediaries for your spiritual growth—other people, methods, or habits—instead of turning directly to God? What would it look like to cut that regress and depend entirely on Him as the sole agent of change in your heart?
?
The argument proves that the agent's efficacy is not added but identical with or necessary to the essence. How does this truth affect how you see your own identity as a servant of God? Are you content to be defined by your connection to Him, or do you seek to add attributes to yourself that make you feel independent? Commit to one action today that reflects that your very existence and power are not separate from your submission to Allah.

Priority is Not a Positive Attribute
Razi refutes the claim that priority is a positive attribute with three arguments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why priority cannot be a real, positive attribute, through three logical arguments.

Core Idea
Priority is a relational concept, not a real property.

Imam Razi addresses the claim that priority (qabliyya) is a positive attribute. He offers three clear arguments to show that priority cannot be an existent quality. This lesson walks through each argument, revealing the logical flaws in treating priority as a real attribute.

Guided Path
1
Understand the claim being refuted
The opponent argues that priority is a positive attribute of Allah. Read the passage to see Razi's response.
2
Identify the three arguments
Find the three numbered arguments in the passage. Notice how each one attacks the idea from a different angle.
The arguments are about non-existence, relation, and analogy.
3
Focus on the second argument
This argument uses the nature of relations. Reflect on why priority and posteriority cannot coexist simultaneously without contradiction.
This is a key logical point.
4
Consider the third argument's analogy
Razi uses the example of 'yesterday' and 'today' to show that non-temporal priority is possible.
This undermines the need for a real attribute.
5
Summarize the lesson
Write a one-sentence conclusion: priority is not a positive attribute because it either attaches to non-existence, implies a contradiction, or is merely relational.
Check your understanding against the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والجواب عن الشبهة الرابعة إن المفهوم من القبلية لا يعقل أن يكون صفة ثبوتية، ويدل عليه وجوه : أحدها: أنكم إن سلمتم أن كل محدث كان عدمه قبل وجوده فقد جعلتم القبلية صفة للعدم وصفة العدم لا يعقل أن تكون موجودة فالقبلية صفة غير موجودة. وثانيها : أن التقدم إضافة لا تعقل إلا بالإضافة إلى التأخر، والمضافان يوجدان معاً، فلو كان التقدم صفة موجودة لاستحال وجودها إلا مع وجود التأخر، وإذا كان حصول التقدم والتأخر معا لزم أن يكون حصول المتقدم والمتأخر معاً، ولكن المعية تنافي في التقدم والتأخر، فإذن القول بأن القبلية صفة موجودة يفضي إلى هذا المحال فيكون محالا. وثالثها: أنا قد دللنا في أول المسألة على أن الأمس متقدم على اليوم، وليس ذلك التقدم بالزمان فلم لا يجوز أن يكون تقدم العدم على الوجود جاريًا مجرى تقدم اليوم على الغد؟
And the answer to the fourth doubt: The concept of priority cannot be conceived as a positive attribute, and this is indicated by arguments: One: If you concede that every originated thing had its non-existence before its existence, you have made priority an attribute of non-existence, and an attribute of non-existence cannot be conceived as existent, so priority is a non-existent attribute. Second: Priority is a relation not conceivable except in relation to posteriority, and the two related things exist together. So if priority were an existent attribute, it would be impossible for it to exist except with the existence of posteriority, and if priority and posteriority occur together, it would necessitate that the prior and the posterior occur together, but simultaneity is incompatible with priority and posteriority. Therefore, saying that priority is an existent attribute leads to this absurdity, so it is absurd. Third: We have demonstrated at the beginning of the issue that yesterday is prior to today, and that priority is not temporal; why then may not the priority of non-existence over existence be like the priority of today over tomorrow?
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the claim that priority (qabliyya) is a real, positive attribute. The author gives three arguments. First: if priority is an attribute, it would attach to non-existence (since non-existence precedes existence), but non-existence cannot have real attributes. Second: priority is a relation, and relations require both relata to exist simultaneously; but if priority exists, it requires posteriority to exist at the same time, which would make the prior and the posterior simultaneous, a contradiction. Third: the prior non-existence is analogous to the priority of 'yesterday' over 'today', which is not temporal priority, so why must it be a real attribute?

Key Terms
القبلية
صفة ثبوتية
التقدم
التأخر
الإضافة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Priority is a real, positive attribute that exists in the subject.
Correction: Priority is a relational concept that cannot be a positive attribute because it either attaches to non-existence, leads to contradiction, or is merely analogous to non-temporal priority.

Checkpoint
What does the second argument say about priority?
A) Priority is an attribute of existence.
B) Priority is a relation that requires both relata to exist together, leading to contradiction.
C) Priority is temporal.
D) Priority is an attribute of non-existence.

Key Takeaway
Priority is not a positive attribute but a relational concept or a non-temporal notion, as shown by three logical arguments.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about Allah's attribute of 'Being First' (al-Awwal), have you ever imagined it as a positive property added to His essence? How does Razi's argument that priority is merely relational reshape your understanding of what it means for Allah to be 'First'? Will you now consciously avoid attributing real, temporal priority to Allah's essence?
?
You just learned that non-existence cannot have attributes. Do you ever catch yourself speaking about 'before creation' as if non-existence were a state with properties? What does this lesson teach you about the danger of giving reality to what is not? How will you guard your speech about the pre-creational state?
?
The second argument shows that if priority were a real attribute, it would force the prior and posterior to coexist—a clear contradiction. Are there any beliefs you hold about Allah that, when examined closely, lead to similar logical impossibilities? Will you commit to testing each of your theological convictions with the same rigor Razi applies here?

Response to Doubt: Existence as Generosity
Razi refutes the fifth doubt about existence as generosity implying priority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the claim that 'giving existence is generosity' does not entail temporal priority, as shown by examples from creation.

Core Idea
Generosity does not force temporal priority; the universe's forms and accidents prove it.

Imam Razi now addresses the fifth doubt, where opponents argue that God's act of giving existence is an act of generosity that must precede its object. Razi counters with a simple but powerful observation: the very act of bringing forms and accidents into existence is also generous, yet they are not prior to God. This lesson unpacks his refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the passage for the fifth doubt carefully. Notice the structure: objection then refutation.
Pay attention to the key terms: الإيجاد and جود.
2
Identify the objection
The objection claims that 'giving existence' (الإيجاد) is generosity (جود), implying that the object of generosity must be temporally prior. Mark this premise.
3
Understand the refutation
Razi points out that the same act of giving existence to forms and accidents is also generous, yet they do not precede God. This breaks the supposed connection between generosity and priority.
The phrase 'فإنه جود ولم يلزم' is crucial.
4
Reflect on the logical move
Razi uses a counterexample from observable reality (forms and accidents) to invalidate the general rule. This is a classic argument from inconsistency.
Consider why this refutes the doubt without needing to prove a different doctrine.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والجواب عن الشبهة الخامسة : وهي قولهم : " الإيجاد جود" نقول: هذا ينتقض بإيجاد هذه الصور والأعراض الحادثة ؛ فإنه جود ولم يلزم من تقدم هذه الصور والأعراض. والجواب عن الشبهة السادسة : لم لا يجوز أن يقال : الفاعل المختار يرجح أحد مقدوريه على الآخر من غير اكتساب كمال ولا رفع يقتضيه، بل محض الإرادة، وبالله التوفيق.
And the answer to the fifth doubt: Which is their saying: 'Giving existence is generosity.' We say: This is refuted by the giving of existence to these forms and accidental attributes; for it is generosity, and it does not necessitate the priority of these forms and accidents. And the answer to the sixth doubt: Why may it not be said that the freely acting agent prefers one of his two possibilities over the other without acquiring perfection or removing a requirement of it, but simply by will? And with God is success.
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage contains two brief responses. First, to the objection that 'giving existence is generosity' implying temporal priority, the author refutes by noting that acts of generating forms and accidents are also generous but do not entail priority. Second, regarding the sixth doubt, the author asserts that the free agent (God) can prefer one of two equally possible actions over another without needing a cause like acquiring perfection or removing a condition; pure will suffices. The lesson ends with a formulaic expression of reliance on God.

Key Terms
الإيجاد
جود
صور
أعراض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: People might think that God's generosity requires that the object of generosity (the world) be temporally prior to the act.
Correction: Razi shows that the same act of giving existence to forms and accidents is generous but does not imply their priority.

Checkpoint
According to the refutation of the fifth doubt, what does the act of giving existence to forms and accidents demonstrate?
A) That the forms and accidents are prior to God.
B) That generosity necessitates priority.
C) That generosity does not entail priority.
D) That the forms and accidents are not generous.

Key Takeaway
Generosity does not force temporal priority; counterexamples from creation invalidate the doubt.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
When you look at the forms and accidents of your own life—your body, your circumstances—do you recognize them as instances of God's generosity that imply no priority on your part? What would change if you truly believed that?

Razi answers the sixth doubt by affirming that God's will alone suffices for choice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why God, as a free agent, can choose between two equally possible actions solely through will, without needing an external cause.

Core Idea
Pure will suffices for God's choice; no acquired perfection or removal is needed.

The sixth doubt challenges God's freedom to choose without a cause. Razi responds by affirming that the free agent (God) can prefer one possibility over another simply by will, without acquiring new perfection or removing a deficiency. This lesson explores that simple yet profound answer.

Guided Path

Identify the doubt's assumption
The doubt likely assumes that a choice requires a motivating cause besides will, such as acquiring perfection or removing a deficiency. Razi rejects that.
3
Understand Razi's positon
Razi asserts that God's preference can be purely based on will (محض الإرادة), without external factors. This upholds God's absolute freedom.
The phrase 'من غير اكتساب كمال ولا رفع يقتضيه' lists the rejected alternatives.
4
Reflect on the implications
If God needed a cause to choose, He would be dependent. Razi's answer defends tawhid and divine omnipotence.
The formula 'وبالله التوفيق' shows reliance on God.

Answers to the Fifth and Sixth Objections
Razi responds to two objections about divine generosity and free choice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi refutes two objections against the temporal priority of non-existence by appealing to divine generosity and free will.

Core Idea
Divine generosity does not imply temporal priority; pure will suffices for choice.

In this passage, Imam Razi tackles two common objections that could undermine arguments about the temporal priority of non-existence. The first objection conflates generosity with logical priority; the second questions the basis of divine choice. Razi's answers reaffirm divine sovereignty and simplicity.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Notice the structure: a short introduction, then two distinct objection-answer pairs.
The passage ends with the pious phrase 'وبالله التوفيق'.
2
Analyze the fifth objection rebuttal
Focus on the first answer. Razi counters the claim that bestowing existence (إيجاد) is generosity (جود) by pointing to the creation of forms and accidents, which are obviously generous but do not entail that the recipient must have existed before.
Key insight: generosity does not logically require temporal priority of non-existence.
3
Analyze the sixth objection rebuttal
Now examine the second answer. The objection questions why a free agent chooses one option over another without additional motive. Razi asserts that pure will (محض الإرادة) is sufficient—no external perfection or requirement is needed.
This defends divine freedom and independence from any external cause.

Commentary
This passage contains the conclusion of the Third Introduction, where Razi answers two objections raised against an earlier argument (likely about the priority of non-existence over existence). The first objection claims that bestowing existence is an act of generosity, implying a relation between donor and recipient. The First Proof: Existence as a Common Predicate
Razi states the second question and presents the first argument for existence as an addition to essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first kalam argument for existence being additional to essence, based on the commonality of existence across all existents.

Core Idea
Existence is a shared predicate; essences are not — so existence must be distinct.

Razi now presents the first of several arguments for the view that existence is an attribute distinct from essence. This argument focuses on the logical observation that existence is a predicate common to all things that are affirmed, while the particularities of each thing's essence are unique. The argument relies on reason's ability to conceive a single concept of affirmation, independent of any specific essence.

Guided Path
1
Background: the second question
Learn why the issue of non-existence branching from existence-essence distinction is significant.
This sets the context for the proof.
2
Read the two positions
Identify al-Ash'ari's view (existence = essence) and the majority view (existence additional).
3
Analyze the first proof
Focus on the claim that existence is a common predicate while essences are not, and the supporting argument about no middle between contradictories.
Notice how the argument uses pure reason, not revelation.
4
Examine the objection
Understand the objector's challenge: either the argument is trivial or it begs the question.
This is a sophisticated objection.
5
Study Razi's reply
See how Razi defends the unicity of the concept of affirmation using reason's ability to conceive it without reference to any specific essence.
This ties back to the core idea.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسألة الثانية
في أن المعدوم ليس بشيء
وهذه المسألة متفرعة على مسألة أخرى وهي أن الوجود هل هو مغاير للماهية أم لا؟ فذهب أبو الحسن الأشعري" إلى أن وجود كل شيء نفس ماهيته وذهب كثير من المتكلمين وجمهور الحكماء إلى أن وجود الشيء وصف مغاير
لماهيته.
واحتج من قال بأن الوجود زائد على الماهية بوجوه : الوجه الأول : أن الوجود وصف مشترك فيه بين الموجودات وخصوصیات
الماهيات غير مشترك فيها بين الموجودات فالوجود مغاير للماهية. وإنما قلنا : إن الوجود وصف مشترك فيه بين الموجودات بوجوه : الأول : أن صريح العقل حاكم بأنه لا واسطة بين طرفي النقيضين، ولولا أن مفهوم الوجود أمر واحد واقع في مقابلة النفي، وإلا لبطل ذلك.
فإن قيل : إن عنيتم بقولكم إنه لا واسطة بين النقيضين أنه لا واسطة بين تحقق تلك الحقيقة وبين لا تحققها فهذا مسلم، ولكن هذا لا يقتضي كون الوجود قدرًا مشتركا بين كل الموجودات، فإن تحقق كل حقيقة عبارة عن خصوصية تلك الحقيقة، وتعين تلك الماهية وإن عنيتم به أن ههنا مفهوما مشتركًا واحدًا بين الموجودات هو المسمى بالموجودية، فهذا هو المصادرة على المطلوب.
قلنا : لا شك في أن العقل يتصور من معنى الثبوت مفهوما ومن معنى السلب
مفهوماً، ويجزم بأنهما لا يجتمعان ولا يرتفعان، وهو عند تصور مفهوم الثبوت ومفهوم السلب لا يفتقر إلى الإشارة إلى ماهية معينة وذلك يوجب كون مفهوم الثبوت أمرًا واحدًا.
The Second Question: That the non-existent is not a thing. This question is branched from another question, which is whether existence is distinct from essence or not. Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari held that the existence of everything is its very essence, while many of the theologians (mutakallimun) and the majority of the philosophers (hukama') held that the existence of a thing is an attribute distinct from its essence. And the one who said that existence is additional to essence argued with proofs: The first proof: that existence is a predicate common among existents, while the particularities of essences are not common among existents, so existence is distinct from essence. We only said that existence is a predicate common among existents in ways: The first: that pure reason judges that there is no middle between the two sides of contradictories, and were it not that the concept of existence is a single thing standing in opposition to negation, then that would be invalid. If it is said: If you mean by your statement that there is no middle between the two contradictories that there is no middle between the realization of that reality and its non-realization, this is granted, but this does not necessitate that existence is a common factor among all existents, for the realization of each reality is an expression of the particularity of that reality and the specification of that essence; and if you mean by it that there is here a single common concept among existents called 'existent-ness' (al-mawjudiyya), this is begging the question (musadara). We say: There is no doubt that reason conceives from the meaning of affirmation (thubut) a concept and from the meaning of negation (salb) a concept, and it judges that they do not combine and do not both disappear, and it, when conceiving the concept of affirmation and the concept of negation, does not need to refer to a specific essence, and that necessitates that the concept of affirmation is a single thing.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage introduces the second major question: 'That the non-existent is not a thing,' which branches from the more fundamental issue of whether existence is distinct from essence. Razi records al-Ash'ari's position (existence = essence) and the majority view (existence is an additional attribute). Then he presents the first proof (al-wajh al-awwal) of the majority: existence is a common predicate among existents, while the particularities of essences are not common, so existence must be distinct. The proof rests on the observation that reason recognizes no middle ground between existence and non-existence, implying a single concept of existence opposed to negation. An objector raises two possible interpretations of 'no middle' — the first is granted but does not prove commonality, the second is circular. Razi replies that reason conceives a single concept of affirmation (thubut) independent of any specific essence, confirming the unicity of the concept of existence.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The argument is about physical existence as a shared property like color.
Correction: The argument is about the logical concept of affirmation (thubut) that is common across all propositions, not a physical property.

Checkpoint
What is the first argument used by those who claim existence is additional to essence?
A) Essences exist independently of existence.
B) Existence is a predicate common among existents, while the particularities of essences are not common.
C) Al-Ash'ari said so.
D) Reason cannot conceive of existence without essence.

Key Takeaway
Existence is a common predicate across all existents, distinct from each unique essence, proven by reason's single concept of affirmation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just read Razi's argument that existence is a single concept common to all things. When you say 'God exists' and 'I exist,' do you truly believe those two statements share the same meaning of 'exists'? Or do you instinctively think God's existence is so different that it cannot be captured by the same word? What does your answer reveal about your understanding of God's nature? Commit to examining whether your heart treats God's existence as fundamentally other or as merely a greater instance of your own.
?
Razi relies on the principle that there is no middle ground between a thing's existence and non-existence. In your own life, are there areas where you try to live in a 'middle' state—neither fully committed to obeying God nor fully neglecting Him? Name one specific habit or relationship where you are avoiding the decisive choice. Will you today take a concrete step to eliminate that middle ground, embracing either wholehearted devotion or clear renunciation?
?
The objector in the passage challenges the assumption that existence is a single concept. Have you ever truly questioned your own assumptions about what it means for something to 'be'? Perhaps you have assumed that 'being' is obvious, yet this lesson shows it is deeply debated. Take five minutes right now to sit in silence and ask yourself: What do I actually mean when I say something 'is'? Let the uncertainty unsettle you, and ask God to grant you clarity on the reality of His existence versus created existence.

The Third Proof: Existence is Additional to Essence
Razi presents the third proof that existence is additional to essence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical structure of Imam Razi's third proof that existence is additional to essence.

Core Idea
If we can conceive an essence without existence, then existence cannot be identical to it.

The third proof is deceptively simple: we can think of an essence while completely ignoring whether it exists or not. If existence were the essence itself or a part of it, this would be impossible. Therefore, existence must be something extra.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof statement
Read the Arabic text of the proof and its literal translation. Notice how Razi states the proof in one concise conditional sentence.
2
Understand the key premise
The premise is that we can be heedless (dhuhul) of existence while conceiving the essence. Ask yourself: is this true for all things? For necessary things?
This premise is considered self-evident by the author.
3
Consider the implication
If existence were the essence or a part, then heedlessness of existence would mean heedlessness of the essence itself, which is impossible because we are actively conceiving the essence.
4
Formulate the proof in your own words
Try to restate the proof as a step-by-step argument. This will help solidify the logic.
The proof relies on the distinction between conception and existence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الثالثة على أن الوجود زائد على الماهية وهو أنه يمكننا أن نعقل الماهية مع الذهول عن وجودها ولو كان الوجود نفس الماهية أو جزءًا من أجزاء الماهية لكان ذلك ممتنعا. فإن قيل : هذه حجة منقوضة على قول الفلاسفة؛ فإن عندهم وجود الباري سبحانه نفس حقيقته، مع أنا نعقل وجوده ولا نعقل ماهيته. وأيضًا فإنا نتصور أن الوجود ما هو؟ ثم نصدق بأن ذلك المفهوم حاصل وكائن واقع والتصور قبل التصديق فيلزم أن يكون تصديقنا بأن الوجود واقع وحاصل دالا على حصول وجود، ويلزم منه التسلسل. وأيضًا: فإنا قد نعقل ذاتين مع الذهول عن كون أحدهما لازما للآخر، أو ملزوما له، أو كون أحدهما مؤثرًا في الآخر، أو أثرًا له، أو كون أحدهما حالا في الآخر، أو محلا له فيلزم أن يكون كون الشيء لازما للآخر وملزوما له، ومؤثرًا فيه وأثرًا له، وحالا فيه ومحلا له زائدًا على الذات، وذلك محال لإفضاء ذلك إلى التسلسل، وأيضًا فهب أن ما ذكرتم يدل على أن الوجود الخارجي زائد على الماهية ولكنه لا يفيد أن الوجود الذهني زائد على الماهية. والجواب : أنه إذا صدق على أحد الأمرين كونه معلومًا وعلى الآخر أنه غير معلوم فلو لم يثبت التغير بينهما، لكان قد صدق على الأمر الواحد أنه معلوم وأنه غير معلوم فيلزم اجتماع النفي والإثبات وإنه محال في بدائه العقول، وإذا كانت هذه المقدمة من أقوى البدهيات كان إيراد النقض عليها تشكيكاً، فلا يستحق الجواب. وأيضا : فعندنا أن وجود الله زائد على ماهيته، وأما تصديقنا بأن الوجود قد وقع فليس المراد منه أن الوجود حصل له وجود آخر، بل المراد منه أن الوجود هل حصل للماهية أم لا؟ وهذا عين الدليل الذي تمسكنا به. وأما حديث اللازمية والملزومية وأمثالها فهي اعتبارات ذهنية بخلاف الوجود الخارجي، فإنه لا يمكن أن يقال : إنه اعتبار ذهني، وإلا لزم أن يقال إنه لا موجود في الأعيان، وأن يقال: وجوده في الأعيان نفس الماهية فحينئذ يرجع ما ذكرتم من اجتماع النفي والإثبات على الشيء الواحد، وهو محال. وأما الوجود الذهني فجوابه أن الماهية كما وجدت في الأذهان عارية عن الوجود الخارجي، فقد وجدت في الأعيان عارية عن الوجود الذهني، وذلك يوجب التغاير.
The third argument that existence is additional to the essence is that we can conceive the essence while being heedless of its existence. If existence were the essence itself or a part of the parts of the essence, that would be impossible. For it is said: This argument is refuted according to the statement of the philosophers, for with them the existence of the Exalted Creator is His very reality, yet we conceive His existence and do not conceive His essence. And also: we imagine what existence is, then we assent that that concept is actual and occurring, and conception is before assent, so it would follow that our assent that existence is actual and occurring indicates the occurrence of existence, leading to infinite regress. And also: we may conceive two essences while being heedless of one being a concomitant of the other, or the other being a concomited, or one being an effect in the other, or an effect of it, or one being in a state in the other, or a locus for it; then it would follow that a thing being a concomitant of another, or a concomited, or an effect in it, or an effect of it, or in a state in it, or a locus for it is additional to the essence, and that is impossible because it leads to infinite regress. And also: suppose what you mention indicates that external existence is additional to the essence, but it does not show that mental existence is additional to the essence. The answer: If 'being known' is true of one of two things and 'being unknown' is true of the other, then if difference between them were not established, it would be true of the same thing that it is known and unknown, necessitating the conjunction of negation and affirmation, which is impossible in the primary intuitions of intellects. Since this premise is among the strongest of self-evident truths, raising a criticism against it is merely sophistry and does not deserve an answer. And also: with us, the existence of God is additional to His essence. As for our assent that existence has occurred, it does not mean that existence has another existence, but rather it means: has existence occurred to the essence or not? This is exactly the argument we relied on. As for the talk of concomitance and being concomited and the like, they are mental considerations, unlike external existence, for it cannot be said that it is a mental consideration, otherwise it would be said that there is no existent in concrete reality, and that its existence in concrete reality is the essence itself; then your conjunction of negation and affirmation on one thing would return, and that is impossible. As for mental existence, its answer is that just as the essence exists in minds stripped of external existence, so it exists in concrete reality stripped of mental existence, and that necessitates difference.
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage presents the third proof that existence is additional to essence, followed by a series of objections and a comprehensive answer. The proof itself is concise: we can conceive an essence while being entirely heedless of its existence. If existence were identical to the essence or a part of it, such heedless conception would be impossible. Therefore, existence must be additional. The first objection comes from the philosophers: they hold that for God, existence is identical to His essence, yet we conceive His existence without conceiving His essence. The second objection argues that if we first conceive existence as a concept and then assent that it actually occurs, conception precedes assent, which would imply an infinite regress. The third objection states that we often conceive two things without knowing their relations (concomitance, causality, etc.), so those relations must be additional, leading to regress. The fourth objection concedes that the proof might show external existence is additional, but not mental existence. The answer addresses all objections. It begins by asserting the self-evident principle that if two things are known and unknown respectively, they must be distinct; otherwise contradiction arises. Since this is a primary intuition, objecting to it is mere sophistry. Then it clarifies that God's existence is indeed additional to His essence according to the author's school. Next, it explains that the assent to existence occurring does not posit a second existence; it merely affirms that existence has occurred to the essence—which is precisely the proof. The relations of concomitance etc. are mental considerations, not real additions, unlike external existence. Finally, regarding mental existence: the essence can be in the mind without external existence, and in concrete reality without mental existence, which shows the two are distinct. Thus the third proof stands.

Key Terms
وجود
ماهية
ذهول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that if something exists, its existence cannot be separated from its essence.
Correction: The proof shows that conceptual separation is possible, indicating real distinction.

Checkpoint
What does Razi claim is possible regarding essence and existence?
A) We cannot conceive an essence without existence.
B) We can conceive an essence while being heedless of its existence.
C) Existence is always part of the essence.
D) Heedlessness is impossible.

Key Takeaway
The third proof relies on the conceptual distinction between essence and existence through the possibility of heedlessness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you often conceive of your future goals and desires while being heedless of whether they truly exist? How does this proof challenge the reality you assign to your ambitions?
?
This proof shows existence is not identical to essence. Consider your own soul: do you ever conflate your temporary existence with your true essence? Why does this distinction matter for your relationship with your Creator?
?
If you can conceive of your own existence (in your mind) without actually existing, what does that imply about the source of your existence? Does this proof push you to reflect on the One whose essence is existence itself?

Answering the Philosophers' Objection: God's Existence
Razi answers the first objection about God's existence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi refutes the objection from the philosophers that for God, existence is identical to essence, yet we conceive His existence without essence.

Core Idea
Two things, one known and one unknown, must be distinct.

The first objection comes from philosophers who hold that for God, existence is His very reality. They argue that we conceive His existence without conceiving His essence, which would contradict the proof if existence were additional. Razi answers with a self-evident principle: if one thing is known and another is unknown, they must be different. Applying this to God, His existence and essence are distinct.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Read the section starting with 'فإن قيل : هذه حجة منقوضة...' up to the part where Razi provides the answer. Identify the objection and the response.
2
Analyze the self-evident principle
Razi says: if one thing is known and another is unknown, they must be different. Why is this considered self-evident? Reflect on it.
This principle is foundational to identity.
3
Apply it to the objection
We conceive God's existence (known) but not His essence (unknown). Therefore, they must be distinct, supporting the proof.
Razi also asserts that in his school (Ash'ari), God's existence is additional to His essence.
4
Appreciate the force of the answer
Razi considers this principle so strong that objecting to it is sophistry. Why might a philosopher reject it?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

The third argument that existence is additional to the essence is that we can conceive the essence while being heedless of its existence. If existence were the essence itself or a part of the parts of the essence, that would be impossible. For it is said: This argument is refuted according to the statement of the philosophers, for with them the existence of the Exalted Creator is His very reality, yet we conceive His existence and do not conceive His essence. How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You acknowledge God's existence, but do you live as though His essence is utterly beyond your grasp? How does that ignorance humble you—or does it simply give you an excuse not to seek Him more deeply? Today, will you spend even five minutes reflecting on one of His attributes to move beyond mere acknowledgment?
?
If a philosopher told you that your knowledge of God's existence automatically gives you knowledge of His essence, would you be tempted to think you've 'figured God out'? Razi insists they are distinct. In what area of your life have you confused knowing about God with truly knowing Him? What will you do to close that gap?
?
The argument hinges on the self-evident principle that known and unknown are different. Is there an area of your faith where you are comfortable with 'not knowing'—perhaps the nature of the afterlife, or the wisdom behind a trial—and that uncertainty erodes your trust? Will you let this principle remind you that not knowing does not mean not real, and still surrender to what you do know?
